      <p><b>Rwanda</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[a]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Rwanda</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region and <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> converge. One of the smallest countries on the African mainland, its capital city is <a href="/wiki/Kigali" title="Kigali">Kigali</a>. Located a few degrees south of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>, Rwanda is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>. It is highly elevated, giving it the soubriquet "land of thousand hills", with its geography dominated by mountains in the west and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> to the east, with numerous lakes throughout the country. The climate is temperate to subtropical, with two rainy seasons and two dry seasons each year. Rwanda has a population of over 12.6&nbsp;million<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> living on 26,338&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (10,169&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of land, and is the most densely populated mainland African country. </p>
      <p>The population is <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_Rwanda" title="Youth in Rwanda">young</a> and predominantly rural. Rwandans are drawn from just one cultural and linguistic group, the <a href="/wiki/Banyarwanda" title="Banyarwanda">Banyarwanda</a>. However, within this group there are three subgroups: the <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Twa" title="Great Lakes Twa">Twa</a>. The Twa are a forest-dwelling <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pygmy people">pygmy people</a> and are often considered descendants of Rwanda's earliest inhabitants. Scholars disagree on the origins of and differences between the Hutu and Tutsi; some believe differences are derived from former social <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">castes</a> within a single people, while others believe the Hutu and Tutsi arrived in the country separately, and from different locations. Christianity is the largest religion in the country; the principal language is <a href="/wiki/Kinyarwanda" title="Kinyarwanda">Kinyarwanda</a>, spoken by most Rwandans, with English and French serving as additional official languages. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Rwanda has a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a> of government. The president is <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">Rwandan Patriotic Front</a> (RPF), who has served continuously since 2000. Today, Rwanda has low levels of corruption compared with neighbouring countries, although human rights organisations report suppression of opposition groups, intimidation and restrictions on freedom of speech. The country has been governed by a strict administrative hierarchy since precolonial times; there are five <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Rwanda" title="Provinces of Rwanda">provinces</a> delineated by borders drawn in 2006. Rwanda is one of only three countries in the world with a female majority in the national parliament, the two other countries being <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">Hunter-gatherers</a> settled the territory in the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Ages</a>, followed later by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a>. The population coalesced first into <a href="/wiki/Clans_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Clans of Rwanda">clans</a> and then into kingdoms. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Rwanda" title="Kingdom of Rwanda">Kingdom of Rwanda</a> dominated from the mid-eighteenth century, with the Tutsi kings conquering others militarily, centralising power and later enacting anti-Hutu policies. <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">Germany</a> colonised Rwanda in 1884 as part of <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgium</a>, which invaded in 1916 during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Both European nations ruled through the kings and perpetuated a pro-Tutsi policy. The Hutu population <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Revolution" title="Rwandan Revolution">revolted</a> in 1959. They massacred numerous Tutsi and ultimately established an independent, Hutu-dominated republic in 1962. A <a href="/wiki/1973_Rwandan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Rwandan coup d'état">1973 military coup</a> saw a change of leadership, but the pro-Hutu policy remained. The Tutsi-led <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">Rwandan Patriotic Front</a> launched a <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Civil_War" title="Rwandan Civil War">civil war</a> in 1990. The presidents of Rwanda and Burundi, both Hutus, were killed when their aircraft was shot down on 6 April 1994. Social tensions erupted in the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">1994 genocide</a> that followed, in which Hutu extremists killed an estimated 500,000–1,000,000 Tutsi and moderate Hutu. The RPF ended the genocide with a military victory. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Rwanda" title="Economy of Rwanda">Rwanda's developing economy</a> suffered heavily in the wake of the 1994 genocide, but has since strengthened. The economy is based mostly on <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>. Coffee and tea are the major <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash crops">cash crops</a> for export. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Rwanda" title="Tourism in Rwanda">Tourism</a> is a fast-growing sector and is now the country's leading foreign exchange earner. Rwanda is one of only two countries in which <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorillas</a> can be visited safely, and visitors pay high prices for gorilla tracking permits. Music and dance are an integral part of Rwandan culture, particularly drums and the highly choreographed <i>intore</i> dance. Traditional arts and crafts are produced throughout the country, including <i><a href="/wiki/Imigongo" title="Imigongo">imigongo</a></i>, a unique cow dung art. </p>
      <p>Rwanda has been governed as a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Rwanda" title="Parliament of Rwanda">bicameral parliament</a> ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">Rwandan Patriotic Front</a> since 1994. The country is member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">COMESA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">OIF</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rwanda" title="History of Rwanda">History of Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Modern human settlement of what is now Rwanda dates from, at the latest, the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, either in the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period around 8000 BC, or in the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Subpluvial" class="mw-redirect" title="Neolithic Subpluvial">long humid period</a> which followed, up to around 3000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200344_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200344-11">[10]</a></sup> Archaeological excavations have revealed evidence of sparse settlement by <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> in the late <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>, followed by a larger population of early <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> settlers, who produced dimpled <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a> and iron tools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDorsey199436_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDorsey199436-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200345_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200345-13">[12]</a></sup> These early inhabitants were the ancestors of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Twa" title="Great Lakes Twa">Twa</a>, aboriginal <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">pygmy</a> hunter-gatherers who remain in Rwanda today.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261-14">[13]</a></sup> Between 700 BC and 1500 AD, a number of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> groups migrated into Rwanda, clearing forest land for agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200358_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200358-15">[14]</a></sup> The forest-dwelling Twa lost much of their habitat and moved to the mountain slopes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200775_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200775-16">[15]</a></sup> Historians have several theories regarding the nature of the Bantu migrations; one theory is that the first settlers were <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> migrated later to form a distinct racial group, possibly of Nilo-hamitic origin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199516_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199516-17">[16]</a></sup> An alternative theory is that the migration was slow and steady, with incoming groups integrating into rather than conquering the existing society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200261-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200258_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200258-18">[17]</a></sup> Under this theory, the Hutu and Tutsi distinction arose later and was a class distinction rather than a racial one.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200369_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200369-19">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShyaka10–11_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShyaka10–11-20">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg/220px-Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg/330px-Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg/440px-Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rwanda_Nyanza_Mwami_Palace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A reconstruction of the ancient King's Palace at <a href="/wiki/Nyanza,_Rwanda" title="Nyanza, Rwanda">Nyanza</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The earliest form of social organisation in the area was the <a href="/wiki/Clans_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Clans of Rwanda">clan</a> (<i>ubwoko</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200388_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200388-21">[20]</a></sup> The clans were not limited to genealogical lineages or geographical area, and most included Hutu, Tutsi, and Twa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien200388–89_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien200388–89-22">[21]</a></sup> From the 15th century, the clans began to coalesce into kingdoms;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003141_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003141-23">[22]</a></sup> by 1700 around eight kingdoms existed in present-day Rwanda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003482_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003482-24">[23]</a></sup> One of these, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Rwanda" title="Kingdom of Rwanda">Kingdom of Rwanda</a>, ruled by the Tutsi <a href="/wiki/Nyiginya" title="Nyiginya">Nyiginya</a> clan, became increasingly dominant from the mid-eighteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003160_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003160-25">[24]</a></sup> The kingdom reached its greatest extent during the nineteenth century under the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Kigeli_IV_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Kigeli IV of Rwanda">Kigeli Rwabugiri</a>. Rwabugiri conquered several smaller states, expanded the kingdom west and north,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003160_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003160-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269-26">[25]</a></sup> and initiated administrative reforms; these included <i><a href="/wiki/Ubuhake" title="Ubuhake">ubuhake</a></i>, in which Tutsi patrons ceded cattle, and therefore privileged status, to Hutu or Tutsi clients in exchange for economic and personal service,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199513–14_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199513–14-27">[26]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uburetwa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Uburetwa (page does not exist)">uburetwa</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corvée">corvée</a> system in which Hutu were forced to work for Tutsi chiefs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269-26">[25]</a></sup> Rwabugiri's changes caused a rift to grow between the Hutu and Tutsi populations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200269-26">[25]</a></sup> The Twa were better off than in pre-Kingdom days, with some becoming dancers in the royal court,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200775_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200775-16">[15]</a></sup> but their numbers continued to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier19956_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier19956-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference_(1884)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Conference (1884)">Berlin Conference of 1884</a> assigned the territory to <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a>, marking the beginning of the colonial era. The explorer <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Adolf_von_G%C3%B6tzen" title="Gustav Adolf von Götzen">Gustav Adolf von Götzen</a> was the first European to significantly explore the country in 1894; he crossed from the south-east to Lake Kivu and met the king.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003217_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003217-29">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier19959_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier19959-30">[29]</a></sup> The Germans did not significantly alter the social structure of the country, but exerted influence by supporting the king and the existing hierarchy and delegating power to local chiefs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199525_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199525-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgian</a> forces took control of Rwanda and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> in 1916, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, beginning a period of more direct colonial rule.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003260_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003260-33">[32]</a></sup> Belgium ruled both Rwanda and Burundi as a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> called <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a>. The Belgians also simplified and centralised the power structure,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003270_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003270-34">[33]</a></sup> and introduced large-scale projects in education, health, public works, and agricultural supervision, including new crops and improved agricultural techniques to try to reduce the incidence of famine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003276–277_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChrétien2003276–277-35">[34]</a></sup> Both the Germans and the Belgians promoted Tutsi supremacy, considering the Hutu and Tutsi different <a href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (classification of human beings)">races</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppiahGates2010450_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppiahGates2010450-36">[35]</a></sup> In 1935, Belgium introduced identity cards labelling each individual as either Tutsi, Hutu, Twa or Naturalised. While it had previously been possible for particularly wealthy Hutu to become honorary Tutsi, the identity cards prevented any further movement between the classes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGourevitch200056–57_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGourevitch200056–57-37">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_(1980).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of President Juvénal Habyarimana arriving with entourage at Andrews Air Force Base, Maryland, USA on 25 September 1980." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg/120px-Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg/180px-Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg/240px-Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_%281980%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="916" data-file-height="1287"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_(1980).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana" title="Juvénal Habyarimana">Juvénal Habyarimana</a>, president from 1973 to 1994
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Belgium continued to rule <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a> (of which Rwanda formed the northern part) as a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trust_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Trust Territories">UN Trust Territory</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, with a mandate to oversee eventual <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(II)_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(II)-38">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(III)_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(III)-39">[38]</a></sup> Tensions escalated between the Tutsi, who favoured early independence, and the Hutu emancipation movement, culminating in the 1959 <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Revolution" title="Rwandan Revolution">Rwandan Revolution</a>: Hutu activists began killing Tutsi and destroying their houses,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindenLinden1977267_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindenLinden1977267-40">[39]</a></sup> forcing more than 100,000 people to seek refuge in neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGourevitch200058–59_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGourevitch200058–59-41">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199551_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199551-42">[41]</a></sup> In 1961, the suddenly pro-Hutu Belgians held a <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_monarchy_referendum,_1961" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan monarchy referendum, 1961">referendum</a> in which the country voted to abolish the monarchy. Rwanda was separated from Burundi and gained independence on 1 July 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199553_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199553-43">[42]</a></sup> which is commemorated as Independence Day, a national holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Cycles of violence followed, with exiled Tutsi attacking from neighbouring countries and the Hutu retaliating with large-scale slaughter and repression of the Tutsi.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199556_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199556-45">[44]</a></sup> In 1973, <a href="/wiki/Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana" title="Juvénal Habyarimana">Juvénal Habyarimana</a> took power in <a href="/wiki/1973_Rwandan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Rwandan coup d'état">a military coup</a>. Pro-Hutu discrimination continued, but there was greater economic prosperity and a reduced amount of violence against Tutsi.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199574–76_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199574–76-46">[45]</a></sup> The Twa remained marginalised, and by 1990 were almost entirely forced out of the forests by the government; many became beggars.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNPO2008History_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNPO2008History-47">[46]</a></sup> Rwanda's population had increased from 1.6&nbsp;million people in 1934 to 7.1&nbsp;million in 1989, leading to competition for land.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier19954_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier19954-48">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg/220px-Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg/330px-Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg/440px-Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nyamata_Memorial_Site_13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Human skulls at the <a href="/wiki/Nyamata" title="Nyamata">Nyamata</a> Genocide Memorial
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">Rwandan Patriotic Front</a> (RPF), a rebel group composed of nearly 500,000 Tutsi refugees, invaded northern Rwanda from their base in Uganda, initiating the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Civil_War" title="Rwandan Civil War">Rwandan Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199593_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199593-49">[48]</a></sup> The group condemned the Hutu-dominated government for failing to democratize and confront the problems facing these refugees. Neither side was able to gain a decisive advantage in the war,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995135–136_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995135–136-50">[49]</a></sup> but by 1992 it had weakened Habyarimana's authority; mass demonstrations forced him into a coalition with the domestic opposition and eventually to sign the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Accords_(Rwanda)" title="Arusha Accords (Rwanda)">Arusha Accords</a> with the RPF.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995190–191_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995190–191-51">[50]</a></sup> The cease-fire ended on 6 April 1994 when <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_and_Cyprien_Ntaryamira" title="Assassination of Juvénal Habyarimana and Cyprien Ntaryamira">Habyarimana's plane was shot down</a> near Kigali Airport, killing him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(III)2010_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(III)2010-52">[51]</a></sup> The shooting down of the plane served as the catalyst for the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>, which began within a few hours. Over the course of approximately 100 days, between 500,000 and 1,000,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenley2007_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenley2007-53">[52]</a></sup> Tutsi and politically moderate Hutu were killed in well-planned attacks on the orders of the interim government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005386_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005386-54">[53]</a></sup> Many Twa were also killed, despite not being directly targeted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNPO2008History_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNPO2008History-47">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Tutsi RPF restarted their offensive, and took control of the country methodically, gaining control of the whole country by mid-July.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005299_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005299-55">[54]</a></sup> The international response to the genocide was limited, with major powers reluctant to strengthen the already overstretched <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Assistance_Mission_for_Rwanda" title="United Nations Assistance Mission for Rwanda">UN peacekeeping force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005364_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2005364-56">[55]</a></sup> When the RPF took over, approximately two million Hutu <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_refugee_crisis" title="Great Lakes refugee crisis">fled to neighbouring countries</a>, in particular <a href="/wiki/Za%C3%AFre" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaïre">Zaïre</a>, fearing reprisals;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995312_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1995312-57">[56]</a></sup> additionally, the RPF-led army was a key belligerent in the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(V)2010_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(V)2010-58">[57]</a></sup> Within Rwanda, a period of reconciliation and justice began, with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_Rwanda" title="International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda">International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda</a> (ICTR) and the reintroduction of <i><a href="/wiki/Gacaca" class="mw-redirect" title="Gacaca">Gacaca</a></i>, a traditional village court system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBowcott2014_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBowcott2014-59">[58]</a></sup> Since 2000 Rwanda's economy,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(X)_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(X)-60">[59]</a></sup> tourist numbers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XI)_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XI)-61">[60]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> have grown rapidly;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(I)2010_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(I)2010-62">[61]</a></sup> between 2006 and 2011 the poverty rate reduced from 57% to 45%,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2012_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2012-63">[62]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> rose from 46.6 years in 2000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(V)20132_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(V)20132-64">[63]</a></sup> to 65.4 years in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Rwanda" title="Politics of Rwanda">Politics of Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Rwanda" title="Foreign relations of Rwanda">Foreign relations of Rwanda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Rwanda">Military of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Paul Kagame, taken in Busan, South Korea, in 2014" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg/170px-Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg/255px-Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg/340px-Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1909" data-file-height="2531"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Kagame_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rwandan President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Rwanda">President of Rwanda</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_98_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_98-66">[65]</a></sup> and has broad powers including creating policy in conjunction with the Cabinet,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_117_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_117-67">[66]</a></sup> exercising the <a href="/wiki/Prerogative_of_mercy_(Rwanda)" class="mw-redirect" title="Prerogative of mercy (Rwanda)">prerogative of mercy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_111_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_111-68">[67]</a></sup> commanding the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Defence_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan Defence Forces">armed forces</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_110_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_110-69">[68]</a></sup> negotiating and ratifying treaties,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_189_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_189-70">[69]</a></sup> signing presidential orders,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_112_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_112-71">[70]</a></sup> and declaring war or a state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_110_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_110-69">[68]</a></sup> The President is elected by popular vote every seven years,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003articles_100–101_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003articles_100–101-72">[71]</a></sup> and appoints the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Rwanda" title="Prime Minister of Rwanda">Prime Minister</a> and all other members of <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of Rwanda">Cabinet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_116_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_116-73">[72]</a></sup> The incumbent president is <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a>, who took office upon the resignation of his predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Pasteur_Bizimungu" title="Pasteur Bizimungu">Pasteur Bizimungu</a>, in 2000. Kagame subsequently won elections in <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_presidential_election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan presidential election, 2003">2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_presidential_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan presidential election, 2010">2010</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELacey2003_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELacey2003-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(IV)2010_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(IV)2010-75">[74]</a></sup> although human rights organisations have criticised these elections as being "marked by increasing political repression and a crackdown on free speech".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch2010_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch2010-76">[75]</a></sup> Article 101 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Rwanda" title="Constitution of Rwanda">constitution</a> had previously limited presidents to two terms in office,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMufulukye2015_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMufulukye2015-77">[76]</a></sup> but this was changed in a <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_constitutional_referendum,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan constitutional referendum, 2015">2015 referendum</a>, which had been brought following receipt of a petition signed by 3.8&nbsp;million Rwandans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUwiringiyamana_(I)2015_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUwiringiyamana_(I)2015-78">[77]</a></sup> Through this change in the constitution, Kagame could stay on as president until 2034.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUwiringiyamana_(II)2015_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUwiringiyamana_(II)2015-79">[78]</a></sup> Kagame was elected for a third term in <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_constitutional_referendum,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan constitutional referendum, 2015">2017</a> with 98.79% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurke2017_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurke2017-80">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch2017_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch2017-81">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The constitution was adopted following a national referendum in 2003, replacing the transitional constitution which had been in place since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPanapress2003_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPanapress2003-82">[81]</a></sup> The constitution mandates a multi-party system of government, with politics based on democracy and elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_52_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_52-83">[82]</a></sup> However, the constitution places conditions on how political parties may operate. Article 54 states that "political organizations are prohibited from basing themselves on race, ethnic group, tribe, clan, region, sex, religion or any other division which may give rise to discrimination".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_54_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_54-84">[83]</a></sup> The government has also enacted laws criminalising genocide ideology, which can include intimidation, defamatory speeches, <a href="/wiki/Genocide_denial" title="Genocide denial">genocide denial</a> and mocking of victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Commission_for_the_Fight_against_Genocide20081_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Commission_for_the_Fight_against_Genocide20081-85">[84]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, these laws effectively make Rwanda a one-party state, as "under the guise of preventing another genocide, the government displays a marked intolerance of the most basic forms of dissent".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoth2009_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoth2009-86">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> is also critical; in its 2014/15 report, Amnesty said that laws against inciting insurrection or trouble among the population had been used to imprison people "for the legitimate exercise of their rights to freedom of association or of expression".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmnesty_International2015311_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmnesty_International2015311-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Rwanda" title="Parliament of Rwanda">Parliament</a> consists of two chambers. It makes legislation and is empowered by the constitution to oversee the activities of the President and the Cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_62_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_62-88">[87]</a></sup> The lower chamber is the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Rwanda">Chamber of Deputies</a>, which has 80 members serving five-year terms. Twenty-four of these seats are reserved for women, elected through a joint assembly of local government officials; another three seats are reserved for youth and disabled members; the remaining 53 are elected by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_76_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_76-89">[88]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_parliamentary_election,_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan parliamentary election, 2018">2018 election</a>, there are 49 female deputies,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKwibuka2018_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKwibuka2018-90">[89]</a></sup> down from 51 in 2013;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunyaneza2013_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunyaneza2013-91">[90]</a></sup> as of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Rwanda is one of only three countries with a female majority in the national parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInter-Parliamentary_Union2020_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInter-Parliamentary_Union2020-92">[91]</a></sup> The upper chamber is the 26-seat <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Rwanda">Senate</a>, whose members are selected by a variety of bodies. A mandatory minimum of 30% of the senators are women. Senators serve eight-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_82_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_82-93">[92]</a></sup> (See also <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality_in_Rwanda" title="Gender equality in Rwanda">Gender equality in Rwanda</a>.) </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaParliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of the Chamber of Deputies with highway in the foreground" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/RwandaParliament.jpg/220px-RwandaParliament.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/RwandaParliament.jpg/330px-RwandaParliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/RwandaParliament.jpg/440px-RwandaParliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaParliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Rwanda">Chamber of Deputies building</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Rwanda's legal system is largely based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Germany" title="Law of Germany">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Belgium" title="Law of Belgium">Belgian</a> <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> systems and <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" title="Customary law">customary law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> The judiciary is independent of the executive branch,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_140_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_140-94">[93]</a></sup> although the President and the Senate are involved in the appointment of Supreme Court judges.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_148_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_148-95">[94]</a></sup> Human Rights Watch have praised the Rwandan government for progress made in the delivery of justice including the abolition of the death penalty,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_WatchWells2008I._Summary_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_WatchWells2008I._Summary-96">[95]</a></sup> but also allege interference in the judicial system by members of the government, such as the politically motivated appointment of judges, misuse of prosecutorial power, and pressure on judges to make particular decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_WatchWells2008VIII._Independence_of_the_Judiciary_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_WatchWells2008VIII._Independence_of_the_Judiciary-97">[96]</a></sup> The constitution provides for two types of courts: ordinary and specialised.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_143_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_143-98">[97]</a></sup> Ordinary courts are the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Rwanda" title="Supreme Court of Rwanda">Supreme Court</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=High_Court_of_Rwanda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="High Court of Rwanda (page does not exist)">High Court</a>, and regional courts, while specialised courts are military courts<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_143_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_143-98">[97]</a></sup> and a system of commercial courts created in 2011 to expedite commercial litigations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKamere2011_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKamere2011-99">[98]</a></sup> Between 2004 and 2012, a system of <a href="/wiki/Gacaca_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="Gacaca courts"><i>Gacaca</i> courts</a> was in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VIII)2015_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VIII)2015-100">[99]</a></sup> <i>Gacaca</i>, a Rwandan traditional court operated by villages and communities, was revived to expedite the trials of genocide suspects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalkerMarch_2004_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalkerMarch_2004-101">[100]</a></sup> The court succeeded in clearing the backlog of genocide cases, but was criticised by human rights groups as not meeting legal fair standard.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(IX)2012_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(IX)2012-102">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda has low corruption levels relative to most other African countries; in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> ranked Rwanda as the fifth cleanest out of 47 countries in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> and 55th cleanest out of 175 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETransparency_International2014_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETransparency_International2014-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAgutamba2014_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAgutamba2014-104">[103]</a></sup> The constitution provides for an <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">Ombudsman</a>, whose duties include prevention and fighting of corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_182_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_182-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Ombudsman_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Ombudsman-106">[105]</a></sup> Public officials (including the President) are required by the constitution to declare their wealth to the Ombudsman and to the public; those who do not comply are suspended from office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAsiimwe2011_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAsiimwe2011-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Rwandan Patriotic Front (RPF) has been the dominant <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> in the country since 1994. The RPF has maintained control of the presidency and the Parliament in national elections, with the party's vote share consistently exceeding 70%. The RPF is seen as a Tutsi-dominated party but receives support from across the country, and is credited with ensuring continued peace, stability, and economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark2010_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark2010-108">[107]</a></sup> Human rights organisation <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> claims that the government suppresses the freedoms of opposition groups; in its 2015 report, Freedom House alleged that the RPF had "prevented new political parties from registering and arrested the leaders of several existing parties, effectively preventing them from fielding candidates" in elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreedom_House2015_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreedom_House2015-109">[108]</a></sup> Amnesty International also claims that the RPF rules Rwanda "without any meaningful opposition".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmnesty_International2015310_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmnesty_International2015310-110">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(I)_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_(I)-111">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">Francophonie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrancophonie_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrancophonie-112">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrainger2007_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrainger2007-113">[112]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher2009_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher2009-114">[113]</a></sup> For many years during the Habyarimana regime, the country maintained close ties with France, as well as Belgium, the former colonial power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199589_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199589-115">[114]</a></sup> Under the RPF government, however, Rwanda has sought closer ties with neighbouring countries in the East African Community and with the English-speaking world. Diplomatic relations with France were suspended in 2006 following the indictment of Rwandan officials by a French judge,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPorter2008_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPorter2008-116">[115]</a></sup> and despite their restoration in 2010, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> relations between the countries remain strained.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEXinhua_News_Agency2015_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEXinhua_News_Agency2015-117">[116]</a></sup> Relations with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (DRC) were tense following Rwanda's involvement in the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(V)2010_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(V)2010-58">[57]</a></sup> the Congolese army alleged Rwandan attacks on their troops, while Rwanda blamed the Congolese government for failing to suppress Hutu rebels in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Kivu" title="South Kivu">South Kivu</a> provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSA_Today2008_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSA_Today2008-118">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAl_Jazeera2007_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAl_Jazeera2007-119">[118]</a></sup> In 2010, the United Nations released a report accusing the Rwandan army of committing wide scale human rights violations and crimes against humanity in the Democratic Republic of the Congo during the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a>, charges denied by the Rwandan government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2010_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2010-120">[119]</a></sup> Relations soured further in 2012, as Kinshasa accused Rwanda of supporting the <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a>, an insurgency in the eastern Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(X)2012_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(X)2012-121">[120]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, peace has been restored and relations are improving.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAgence_Africaine_de_Presse2015_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAgence_Africaine_de_Presse2015-122">[121]</a></sup> Rwanda's relationship with <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> was also tense for much of the 2000s following a 1999 clash between the two countries' armies as they backed opposing rebel groups in the Second Congo War,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeuler2011_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeuler2011-123">[122]</a></sup> but improved significantly in the early 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VI)2011_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VI)2011-124">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaboja2015_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaboja2015-125">[124]</a></sup> In 2019, relations between the two countries deteriorated, with Rwanda closing its borders with Uganda.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi_inspecting_the_Guard_of_Honour,_on_his_arrival,_at_Kigali_International_Airport,_Rwanda_on_July_23,_2018._The_President_of_Rwanda,_Mr._Paul_Kagame_is_also_seen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_inspecting_the_Guard_of_Honour%2C_on_his_arrival%2C_at_Kigali_International_Airport%2C_Rwanda_on_July_23%2C_2018._The_President_of_Rwanda%2C_Mr._Paul_Kagame_is_also_seen.JPG/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_inspecting_the_Guard_of_Honour%2C_on_his_arrival%2C_at_Kigali_International_Airport%2C_Rwanda_on_July_23%2C_2018._The_President_of_Rwanda%2C_Mr._Paul_Kagame_is_also_seen.JPG/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_inspecting_the_Guard_of_Honour%2C_on_his_arrival%2C_at_Kigali_International_Airport%2C_Rwanda_on_July_23%2C_2018._The_President_of_Rwanda%2C_Mr._Paul_Kagame_is_also_seen.JPG/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1381"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi_inspecting_the_Guard_of_Honour,_on_his_arrival,_at_Kigali_International_Airport,_Rwanda_on_July_23,_2018._The_President_of_Rwanda,_Mr._Paul_Kagame_is_also_seen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The RDF providing a guard of honour.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Rwanda Defence Force (RDF) is the national army of Rwanda. Largely composed of former <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan Patriotic Army">Rwandan Patriotic Army</a> (RPA) soldiers, it includes the Rwanda Land Force, Rwanda Air Force and specialised units.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Defence_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Defence-128">[127]</a></sup> After the successful conquest of the country in 1994 in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">Rwandan Patriotic Front</a> decided to split the RPF into a political division (which retained the RPF name) and the RDF, a military division which was to serve as the official army of the Rwandan state. Defence spending continues to represent an important share of the national budget, largely due to continuing security problems along the frontiers with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> and lingering concerns about <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>'s intentions towards its former ally. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decentralization_in_Rwanda" title="Decentralization in Rwanda">Decentralization in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaGeoProvinces.png" class="image"><img alt="Map of Rwanda showing the five provinces in various colours, as well as major cities, lakes, rivers, and areas of neighbouring countries" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/RwandaGeoProvinces.png/220px-RwandaGeoProvinces.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/RwandaGeoProvinces.png 1.5x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="317"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaGeoProvinces.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Provinces of Rwanda
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Rwanda has been governed by a strict hierarchy since precolonial times.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOAU200014_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOAU200014-129">[128]</a></sup> Before colonisation, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_Rwanda" title="List of kings of Rwanda">King</a> (<i>Mwami</i>) exercised control through a system of provinces, districts, hills, and neighbourhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvern20045_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvern20045-130">[129]</a></sup> The current constitution divides Rwanda into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Rwanda" title="Provinces of Rwanda">provinces</a> (<i lang="rw" title="Kinyarwanda-language text">intara</i>), <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rwanda" title="Districts of Rwanda">districts</a> (<i lang="rw" title="Kinyarwanda-language text">uturere</i>), cities, municipalities, towns, <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Rwanda" title="Sectors of Rwanda">sectors</a> (<i lang="rw" title="Kinyarwanda-language text">imirenge</i>), cells (<i lang="rw" title="Kinyarwanda-language text">utugari</i>), and villages (<i lang="rw" title="Kinyarwanda-language text">imidugudu</i>); the larger divisions, and their borders, are established by Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_3_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_3-131">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The five provinces act as intermediaries between the national government and their constituent districts to ensure that national policies are implemented at the district level. The "Rwanda Decentralisation Strategic Framework" developed by the Ministry of Local Government assigns to provinces the responsibility for "coordinating governance issues in the Province, as well as monitoring and evaluation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20078_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20078-132">[131]</a></sup> Each province is headed by a governor, appointed by the President and approved by the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthern_Province_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthern_Province-133">[132]</a></sup> The districts are responsible for coordinating public service delivery and economic development. They are divided into sectors, which are responsible for the delivery of public services as mandated by the districts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20079_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20079-134">[133]</a></sup> Districts and sectors have directly elected councils, and are run by an executive committee selected by that council.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC2004_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC2004-135">[134]</a></sup> The cells and villages are the smallest political units, providing a link between the people and the sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20079_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20079-134">[133]</a></sup> All adult resident citizens are members of their local cell council, from which an executive committee is elected.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC2004_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC2004-135">[134]</a></sup> The city of <a href="/wiki/Kigali" title="Kigali">Kigali</a> is a provincial-level authority, which coordinates urban planning within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20078_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINALOC20078-132">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The present borders were drawn in 2006 with the aim of decentralising power and removing associations with the old system and the genocide. The previous structure of twelve provinces associated with the largest cities was replaced with five provinces based primarily on geography.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(I)2006_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(I)2006-136">[135]</a></sup> These are <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Rwanda" title="Northern Province, Rwanda">Northern Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Province,_Rwanda" title="Southern Province, Rwanda">Southern Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Rwanda" title="Eastern Province, Rwanda">Eastern Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Province,_Rwanda" title="Western Province, Rwanda">Western Province</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kigali_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Kigali Province">Municipality of Kigali</a> in the centre. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Rwanda" title="Geography of Rwanda">Geography of Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Rwanda">Climate of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KageraRuvubu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of confluence of the Kagera and the Ruvubu, with the Rwanda-Tanzania border post in foreground, taken from a nearby hilltop" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/KageraRuvubu.jpg/220px-KageraRuvubu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/KageraRuvubu.jpg/330px-KageraRuvubu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/KageraRuvubu.jpg/440px-KageraRuvubu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KageraRuvubu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kagera_River" title="Kagera River">Kagera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruvubu_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruvubu River">Ruvubu</a> rivers, part of the upper <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 26,338 square kilometres (10,169&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Rwanda is the world's 149th-largest country,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(II)_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(II)-137">[136]</a></sup> and the fourth smallest on the African mainland after <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(II)_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(II)-137">[136]</a></sup> It is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichards1994_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichards1994-138">[137]</a></sup> The entire country is at a high altitude: the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_lowest_point" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by lowest point">lowest point</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Rusizi_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rusizi River">Rusizi River</a> at 950 metres (3,117&nbsp;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> Rwanda is located in Central/Eastern Africa, and is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> It lies a few degrees south of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> and is <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004-139">[138]</a></sup> The capital, Kigali, is located near the centre of Rwanda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica2010-140">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Congo-Nile_Divide" title="Congo-Nile Divide">watershed</a> between the major <a href="/wiki/Congo_Basin" title="Congo Basin">Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nile_Basin" title="Nile Basin">Nile</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basins</a> runs from north to south through Rwanda, with around 80% of the country's area draining into the Nile and 20% into the Congo via the <a href="/wiki/Rusizi_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rusizi River">Rusizi River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENile_Basin_Initiative2010_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENile_Basin_Initiative2010-141">[140]</a></sup> The country's longest river is the <a href="/wiki/Nyabarongo_River_Wetlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyabarongo River Wetlands">Nyabarongo</a>, which rises in the south-west, flows north, east, and southeast before merging with the <a href="/wiki/Ruvubu_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruvubu River">Ruvubu</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Kagera_River" title="Kagera River">Kagera</a>; the Kagera then flows due north along the eastern border with Tanzania. The Nyabarongo-Kagera eventually drains into <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>, and its source in Nyungwe Forest is a contender for the as-yet undetermined overall <a href="/wiki/Source_(river_or_stream)" class="mw-redirect" title="Source (river or stream)">source</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(II)2006_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(II)2006-142">[141]</a></sup> Rwanda has many lakes, the largest being <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a>. This lake occupies the floor of the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> along most of the length of Rwanda's western border, and with a maximum depth of 480 metres (1,575&nbsp;ft),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJørgensen200593_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJørgensen200593-143">[142]</a></sup> it is one of the twenty <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_by_depth" title="List of lakes by depth">deepest lakes in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006153_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006153-144">[143]</a></sup> Other sizeable lakes include <a href="/wiki/Lake_Burera" title="Lake Burera">Burera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ruhondo" title="Lake Ruhondo">Ruhondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Muhazi" title="Lake Muhazi">Muhazi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Rweru" title="Lake Rweru">Rweru</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ihema" title="Lake Ihema">Ihema</a>, the last being the largest of a string of lakes in the eastern plains of <a href="/wiki/Akagera_National_Park" title="Akagera National Park">Akagera National Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHodd1994522_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHodd1994522-145">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of a lake with one of the Virunga mountains behind, partially in cloud" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg/220px-RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg/330px-RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg/440px-RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RwandaVolcanoAndLake_cropped2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lake and volcano in the <a href="/wiki/Virunga_Mountains" title="Virunga Mountains">Virunga Mountains</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mountains dominate central and western Rwanda and the country is sometimes called "Pays des mille collines" in French ("Land of a thousand hills").<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> They are part of the Albertine Rift Mountains that flank the Albertine branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>, which runs from north to south along Rwanda's western border.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWWF2001Location_and_General_Description_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWWF2001Location_and_General_Description-147">[146]</a></sup> The highest peaks are found in the <a href="/wiki/Virunga_Mountains" title="Virunga Mountains">Virunga</a> volcano chain in the northwest; this includes <a href="/wiki/Mount_Karisimbi" title="Mount Karisimbi">Mount Karisimbi</a>, Rwanda's highest point, at 4,507 metres (14,787&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMehtaKatee200537_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMehtaKatee200537-148">[147]</a></sup> This western section of the country lies within the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift_montane_forests" title="Albertine Rift montane forests">Albertine Rift montane forests</a> ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWWF2001Location_and_General_Description_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWWF2001Location_and_General_Description-147">[146]</a></sup> It has an elevation of 1,500 to 2,500 metres (4,921 to 8,202&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunyakaziNtagaramba20057_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunyakaziNtagaramba20057-149">[148]</a></sup> The centre of the country is predominantly rolling hills, while the eastern border region consists of <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a>, plains and swamps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunyakaziNtagaramba200518_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunyakaziNtagaramba200518-150">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>Rwanda has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical highland</a> climate, with lower temperatures than are typical for equatorial countries because of its high elevation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004-139">[138]</a></sup> Kigali, in the centre of the country, has a typical daily temperature range between 12 and 27&nbsp;°C (54 and 81&nbsp;°F), with little variation through the year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Meteorological_Organization_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Meteorological_Organization-151">[150]</a></sup> There are some temperature variations across the country; the mountainous west and north are generally cooler than the lower-lying east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBest_Country_Reports2007_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBest_Country_Reports2007-152">[151]</a></sup> There are two rainy seasons in the year; the first runs from February to June and the second from September to December. These are separated by two <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry seasons</a>: the major one from June to September, during which there is often no rain at all, and a shorter and less severe one from December to February.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200710_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200710-153">[152]</a></sup> Rainfall varies geographically, with the west and northwest of the country receiving more precipitation annually than the east and southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle20071_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle20071-154">[153]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> has caused a change in the pattern of the rainy seasons. According to a report by the Strategic Foresight Group, change in climate has reduced the number of rainy days experienced during a year, but has also caused an increase in frequency of torrential rains.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrategic_Foresight_Group201329_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrategic_Foresight_Group201329-155">[154]</a></sup> Both changes have caused difficulty for farmers, decreasing their productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBucyensenge2014_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBucyensenge2014-156">[155]</a></sup> Strategic Foresight also characterise Rwanda as a fast warming country, with an increase in average temperature of between 0.7&nbsp;°C to 0.9&nbsp;°C over fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrategic_Foresight_Group201329_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrategic_Foresight_Group201329-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Rwanda" title="Wildlife of Rwanda">Wildlife of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg/220px-Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg/330px-Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg/440px-Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6720" data-file-height="4480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_from_Susa_Group_in_Karisimbi_thicket_of_Volcanoes_National_Park_in_Rwanda._Emmanuel_Kwizera.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Volcanoes_National_Park" title="Volcanoes National Park">Volcanoes National Park</a> is the home of the largest population of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Gorillas" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain Gorillas">Mountain Gorillas</a> in the world.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting four Topis on a hillside in Akagera, with another hill and a lake visible in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg/220px-Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg/330px-Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg/440px-Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6528" data-file-height="4336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Topi_in_Akagera_National_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Topi" title="Topi">Topis</a> in Akagera National Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In prehistoric times <a href="/wiki/Montane_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Montane forest">montane forest</a> occupied one-third of the territory of present-day Rwanda.
