Naturally occurring vegetation is now mostly restricted to the three <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_Rwanda" title="National parks of Rwanda">National Parks</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(agriculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrace (agriculture)">terraced agriculture</a> dominating the rest of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth20063–4_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth20063–4-157">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nyungwe_Forest" title="Nyungwe Forest">Nyungwe</a>, the largest remaining tract of forest, contains 200 species of tree as well as <a href="/wiki/Orchid" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchid">orchids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Begonia" title="Begonia">begonias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200711_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200711-158">[157]</a></sup> Vegetation in the <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes_National_Park" title="Volcanoes National Park">Volcanoes National Park</a> is mostly <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a> and moorland, with small areas of forest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth20063–4_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth20063–4-157">[156]</a></sup> By contrast, Akagera has a <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> ecosystem in which <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a> dominates the flora. There are several rare or endangered plant species in Akagera, including <i><a href="/wiki/Markhamia_lutea" title="Markhamia lutea">Markhamia lutea</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Eulophia_guineensis" title="Eulophia guineensis">Eulophia guineensis</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREMA_(Chapter_5)20093_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREMA_(Chapter_5)20093-159">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg/170px-Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg/255px-Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg/340px-Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="693" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Talk_-_Flickr_-_askmeaks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Giraffe in Akagera National Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The greatest diversity of large mammals is found in the three National Parks, which are designated conservation areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Rwanda_(II)_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Rwanda_(II)-160">[159]</a></sup> Akagera contains typical savanna animals such as giraffes and elephants,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERDB_(III)_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERDB_(III)-161">[160]</a></sup> while Volcanoes is home to an estimated one-third of the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorilla</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERDB_(I)2010_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERDB_(I)2010-162">[161]</a></sup> Nyungwe Forest boasts thirteen primate species including <a href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" class="mw-redirect" title="Common chimpanzee">common chimpanzees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black-and-white_colobus" title="Black-and-white colobus">Ruwenzori colobus</a> arboreal monkeys; the Ruwenzori colobus move in groups of up to 400 individuals, the largest troop size of any primate in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006140_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006140-163">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda's population of <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a> was destroyed in the aftermath of the genocide of 1994, as national parks were turned into camps for displaced people and remaining animals were poisoned by cattle herders. In June 2015, two South African parks donated seven lions to <a href="/wiki/Akagera_National_Park" title="Akagera National Park">Akagera National Park</a>, reestablishing a lion population in Rwanda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2015_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2015-164">[163]</a></sup> The lions were held initially in a fenced off area of the park, and then collared and released into the wild a month later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_New_Times2015_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_New_Times2015-165">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 670 <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Rwanda" title="List of birds of Rwanda">bird species in Rwanda</a>, with variation between the east and the west.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200715_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200715-166">[165]</a></sup> Nyungwe Forest, in the west, has 280 recorded species, of which 26 are endemic to the Albertine Rift;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200715_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200715-166">[165]</a></sup> endemic species include the <a href="/wiki/Rwenzori_turaco" title="Rwenzori turaco">Rwenzori turaco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Handsome_spurfowl" title="Handsome spurfowl">handsome spurfowl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWCS_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWCS-167">[166]</a></sup> Eastern Rwanda, by contrast, features savanna birds such as the <a href="/wiki/Black-headed_gonolek" title="Black-headed gonolek">black-headed gonolek</a> and those associated with swamps and lakes, including <a href="/wiki/Stork" title="Stork">storks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crane_(bird)" title="Crane (bird)">cranes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing200715_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing200715-166">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recent entomological work in the country has revealed a rich diversity of <a href="/wiki/Praying_mantises" class="mw-redirect" title="Praying mantises">praying mantises</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETedrow2015_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETedrow2015-168">[167]</a></sup> including a new species <i>Dystacta tigrifrutex</i>, dubbed the "bush tiger mantis".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaynard2014_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaynard2014-169">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda contains three terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift_montane_forests" title="Albertine Rift montane forests">Albertine Rift montane forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Basin_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Basin forest-savanna mosaic">Victoria Basin forest-savanna mosaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ruwenzori-Virunga_montane_moorlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruwenzori-Virunga montane moorlands">Ruwenzori-Virunga montane moorlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-170">[169]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 3.85/10, ranking it 139th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-171">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Rwanda" title="Economy of Rwanda">Economy of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of four drying racks containing white coloured unroasted coffee beans" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg/220px-MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg/330px-MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg/440px-MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MarabaCoffeeDryingRacks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coffee beans drying in <a href="/wiki/Maraba_coffee" title="Maraba coffee">Maraba</a>. Coffee is one of Rwanda's major cash crops.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Rwanda's economy suffered heavily during the 1994 genocide, with widespread loss of life, failure to maintain infrastructure, looting, and neglect of important cash crops. This caused a large drop in GDP and destroyed the country's ability to attract private and external investment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> The economy has since strengthened, with per-capita GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>) estimated at <a href="/wiki/Geary%E2%80%93Khamis_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Geary–Khamis dollar">$</a>2,444 in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-172">[171]</a></sup> compared with $416 in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIMF_(I)_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIMF_(I)-173">[172]</a></sup> Major export markets include China, Germany, and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> The economy is managed by the central <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Rwanda" title="National Bank of Rwanda">National Bank of Rwanda</a> and the currency is the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_franc" title="Rwandan franc">Rwandan franc</a>; in December 2019, the exchange rate was 910 francs to one United States dollar.<sup id="cite_ref-0r_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-0r-174">[173]</a></sup> Rwanda joined the East African Community in 2007, and has ratified a plan for <a href="/wiki/Monetary_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Monetary union">monetary union</a> amongst the five member nations,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAsiimwe2014_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAsiimwe2014-175">[174]</a></sup> which could eventually lead to a common <a href="/wiki/East_African_shilling#Second_East_African_shilling" title="East African shilling">East African shilling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavelle2008_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavelle2008-176">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda is a country of few natural resources,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004-139">[138]</a></sup> and the economy is based mostly on <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a> by local farmers using simple tools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFAO_/_WFP1997_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFAO_/_WFP1997-177">[176]</a></sup> An estimated 90% of the working population farms, and agriculture constituted an estimated 32.5% of GDP in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> Farming techniques are basic, with small plots of land and steep slopes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa-178">[177]</a></sup> Since the mid-1980s, farm sizes and food production have been decreasing, due in part to the resettlement of displaced people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWRI2006_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWRI2006-179">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004_139-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2004-139">[138]</a></sup> Despite Rwanda's fertile ecosystem, food production often does not keep pace with population growth, and food imports are required,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup>But in recent years, with the growth of agriculture, the situation has improved. </p>
      <p>Subsistence crops grown in the country include <a href="/wiki/Matoke" title="Matoke">matoke</a> (green bananas), which occupy more than a third of the country's farmland,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa-178">[177]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa_178-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa-178">[177]</a></sup> Coffee and tea are the major cash crops for export, with the high altitudes, steep slopes and volcanic soils providing favourable conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa_178-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOur_Africa-178">[177]</a></sup> Reports have established that more than 400,000 Rwandans make their living from coffee plantation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETumwebaze2016_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETumwebaze2016-180">[179]</a></sup> Reliance on agricultural exports makes Rwanda vulnerable to shifts in their prices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWTO2004_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWTO2004-181">[180]</a></sup> Animals raised in Rwanda include cows, goats, sheep, pigs, chicken, and rabbits, with geographical variation in the numbers of each.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINAGRI2006_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINAGRI2006-182">[181]</a></sup> Production systems are mostly traditional, although there are a few intensive dairy farms around Kigali.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINAGRI2006_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINAGRI2006-182">[181]</a></sup> Shortages of land and water, insufficient and poor-quality feed, and regular disease epidemics with insufficient veterinary services are major constraints that restrict output. Fishing takes place on the country's lakes, but stocks are very depleted, and live fish are being imported in an attempt to revive the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENamata2008_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENamata2008-183">[182]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting female adult gorilla with a baby on her shoulders, surrounded by green foliage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/220px-Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/330px-Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/440px-Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gorilla_mother_and_baby_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">Mountain gorillas</a> in Volcanoes National Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The industrial sector is small, contributing 14.8% of GDP in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> Products manufactured include cement, agricultural products, small-scale beverages, soap, furniture, shoes, plastic goods, textiles and cigarettes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> Rwanda's mining industry is an important contributor, generating US$93&nbsp;million in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2009_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2009-184">[183]</a></sup> Minerals mined include <a href="/wiki/Cassiterite" title="Cassiterite">cassiterite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolframite" title="Wolframite">wolframite</a>, gold, and <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a>, which is used in the manufacture of electronic and communication devices such as mobile phones.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2009_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2009-184">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDelawala2001_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDelawala2001-185">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda's <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> suffered during the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">late-2000s recession</a> as bank lending, foreign aid projects and investment were reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENantaba2010_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENantaba2010-186">[185]</a></sup> The sector rebounded in 2010, becoming the country's largest sector by economic output and contributing 43.6% of the country's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> Key tertiary contributors include banking and finance, wholesale and retail trade, hotels and restaurants, transport, storage, communication, insurance, real estate, business services and public administration including education and health.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENantaba2010_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENantaba2010-186">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Rwanda" title="Tourism in Rwanda">Tourism</a> is one of the fastest-growing economic resources and became the country's leading foreign exchange earner in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2008_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukaaya2008-187">[186]</a></sup> In spite of the genocide's legacy, the country is increasingly perceived internationally as a safe destination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENielsenSpenceley20106_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENielsenSpenceley20106-188">[187]</a></sup> The number of tourist arrivals in 2013 was 864,000 people, up from 504,000 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XI)_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XI)-61">[60]</a></sup> Revenue from tourism was US$303&nbsp;million in 2014, up from just US$62&nbsp;million in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKT_Press2015_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKT_Press2015-189">[188]</a></sup> The largest contributor to this revenue was <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorilla</a> tracking, in the Volcanoes National Park;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKT_Press2015_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKT_Press2015-189">[188]</a></sup> Rwanda is one of only three countries in which <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorillas</a> can be visited safely; the gorillas attract thousands of visitors per year, who are prepared to pay high prices for permits.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENielsenSpenceley20102_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENielsenSpenceley20102-190">[189]</a></sup> Other attractions include Nyungwe Forest, home to chimpanzees, Ruwenzori colobus and other primates, the resorts of Lake Kivu, and Akagera, a small <a href="/wiki/Savanna_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Savanna reserve">savanna reserve</a> in the east of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERDB_(II)_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERDB_(II)-191">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">Media and communications</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Rwanda" title="Telecommunications in Rwanda">Telecommunications in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The largest radio and television stations are state-run, and the majority of newspapers are owned by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015-192">[191]</a></sup> Most Rwandans have access to radio; during the 1994 genocide, the radio station <a href="/wiki/Radio_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision_Libre_des_Mille_Collines" title="Radio Télévision Libre des Mille Collines">Radio Télévision Libre des Mille Collines</a> broadcast across the country, and helped to fuel the killings through anti-Tutsi propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015-192">[191]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the state-run <a href="/wiki/Radio_Rwanda" title="Radio Rwanda">Radio Rwanda</a> is the largest station and the main source of news throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015_192-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015-192">[191]</a></sup> Television access is limited, with most homes not having their own set.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGasore2014_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGasore2014-193">[192]</a></sup> The government rolled out <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital television</a> in 2014, and a year later there were seven national stations operating, up from just one in the pre-2014 analogue era.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOpobo2015_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOpobo2015-194">[193]</a></sup> The press is tightly restricted, and newspapers routinely self-censor to avoid government reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015_192-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(VII)2015-192">[191]</a></sup> Nonetheless, publications in Kinyarwanda, English, and French critical of the government are widely available in Kigali. Restrictions were increased in the run-up to the Rwandan presidential election of 2010, with two independent newspapers, <i>Umuseso</i> and <i>Umuvugizi</i>, being suspended for six months by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=High_Media_Council_(Rwanda)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="High Media Council (Rwanda) (page does not exist)">High Media Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReporters_Without_Borders2010_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReporters_Without_Borders2010-195">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's oldest telecommunications group, <a href="/wiki/Rwandatel" title="Rwandatel">Rwandatel</a>, went into liquidation in 2011, having been 80% owned by Libyan company <a href="/w/index.php?title=LAP_Green&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="LAP Green (page does not exist)">LAP Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMugisha2013_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMugisha2013-196">[195]</a></sup> The company was acquired in 2013 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Liquid_Telecom&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Liquid Telecom (page does not exist)">Liquid Telecom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthwood2013_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthwood2013-197">[196]</a></sup> a company providing telecommunications and <a href="/wiki/Fibre_optic" class="mw-redirect" title="Fibre optic">fibre optic</a> networks across eastern and southern Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMugwe2013_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMugwe2013-198">[197]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Liquid Telecom provides <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">landline</a> service to 30,968 subscribers, with mobile operator <a href="/wiki/MTN_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="MTN Rwanda">MTN Rwanda</a> serving an additional 15,497 fixed line subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERURA20156_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERURA20156-199">[198]</a></sup> Landlines are mostly used by government institutions, banks, <a href="/wiki/Non_Government_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Non Government Organisation">NGOs</a> and embassies, with private subscription levels low.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMajyambere2010_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajyambere2010-200">[199]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> penetration in the country is 72.6%,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERURA20155_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERURA20155-201">[200]</a></sup> up from 41.6% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERURA20113_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERURA20113-202">[201]</a></sup> MTN Rwanda is the leading provider, with 3,957,986 subscribers, followed by <a href="/wiki/Tigo" class="mw-redirect" title="Tigo">Tigo</a> with 2,887,328, and <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Bharti Airtel</a> with 1,336,679.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERURA20156_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERURA20156-199">[198]</a></sup> Rwandatel has also previously operated a mobile phone network, but the industry regulator revoked its licence in April 2011, following the company's failure to meet agreed investment commitments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButera2011_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButera2011-203">[202]</a></sup> Internet penetration is low but rising rapidly; in 2015 there were 12.8 internet users per 100 people,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERURA20155_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERURA20155-201">[200]</a></sup> up from 2.1 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(II)_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(II)-204">[203]</a></sup> In 2011, a 2,300 kilometres (1,400&nbsp;mi) fibre-optic telecommunications network was completed, intended to provide broadband services and facilitate electronic commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReuters2011_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReuters2011-205">[204]</a></sup> This network is connected to <a href="/wiki/SEACOM_(African_cable_system)" title="SEACOM (African cable system)">SEACOM</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">submarine</a> fibre-optic cable connecting communication carriers in southern and eastern Africa. Within Rwanda the cables run along major roads, linking towns around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReuters2011_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReuters2011-205">[204]</a></sup> Mobile provider MTN also runs a <a href="/wiki/Wireless_internet" class="mw-redirect" title="Wireless internet">wireless internet</a> service accessible in most areas of Kigali via pre-paid subscription.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButera2010_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButera2010-206">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2019, <a href="/wiki/Mara_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mara Corporation">Mara Corporation</a> launched the first African made smartphone in Rwanda.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Rwanda" title="Transport in Rwanda">Transport in Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Rwanda" title="Energy in Rwanda">Energy in Rwanda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Rwanda" title="Water supply and sanitation in Rwanda">Water supply and sanitation in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:WaterPumpRwanda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting one adult and five children filling jerrycans at a rural metal water pump with concrete base, at the bottom of a steep rocky hillside" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/WaterPumpRwanda.jpg/220px-WaterPumpRwanda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/WaterPumpRwanda.jpg/330px-WaterPumpRwanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/WaterPumpRwanda.jpg/440px-WaterPumpRwanda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:WaterPumpRwanda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rural water pump
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Rwandan government prioritised funding of water supply development during the 2000s, significantly increasing its share of the national budget.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIDA2009_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIDA2009-208">[207]</a></sup> This funding, along with donor support, caused a rapid increase in access to safe water; in 2015, 74% of the population had access to safe water,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015-209">[208]</a></sup> up from about 55% in 2005;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIDA2009_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIDA2009-208">[207]</a></sup> the government has committed to increasing this to 100% by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015-209">[208]</a></sup> The country's water infrastructure consists of urban and rural systems that deliver water to the public, mainly through standpipes in rural areas and private connections in urban areas. In areas not served by these systems, hand pumps and managed springs are used.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINECOFIN200225–26_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINECOFIN200225–26-210">[209]</a></sup> Despite rainfall exceeding 750 millimetres (30&nbsp;in) annually in most of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerryLewisWilliams1990533_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerryLewisWilliams1990533-211">[210]</a></sup> little use is made of <a href="/wiki/Rainwater_harvesting" title="Rainwater harvesting">rainwater harvesting</a>, and residents are forced to use water very sparingly, relative to usage in other African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmutesi2015-209">[208]</a></sup> Access to <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Rwanda" title="Water supply and sanitation in Rwanda">sanitation</a> remains low; the United Nations estimates that in 2006, 34% of urban and 20% of rural dwellers had access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083-212">[211]</a></sup> Kigali is one of the cleanest cities in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> Government policy measures to improve sanitation are limited, focusing only on urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083-212">[211]</a></sup> The majority of the population, both urban and rural, use public shared <a href="/wiki/Pit_latrine" title="Pit latrine">pit latrines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083_212-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(I)20083-212">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda's electricity supply was, until the early 2000s, generated almost entirely from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> sources; power stations on Lakes <a href="/wiki/Lake_Burera" title="Lake Burera">Burera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ruhondo" title="Lake Ruhondo">Ruhondo</a> provided 90% of the country's electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20113_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20113-214">[213]</a></sup> A combination of below average rainfall and human activity, including the draining of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugezi_wetlands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rugezi wetlands (page does not exist)">Rugezi wetlands</a> for cultivation and grazing, caused the two lakes' water levels to fall from 1990 onwards; by 2004 levels were reduced by 50%, leading to a sharp drop in output from the power stations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115-215">[214]</a></sup> This, coupled with increased demand as the economy grew, precipitated a shortfall in 2004 and widespread <a href="/wiki/Loadshedding" class="mw-redirect" title="Loadshedding">loadshedding</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115-215">[214]</a></sup> As an emergency measure, the government installed <a href="/wiki/Diesel_generator" title="Diesel generator">diesel generators</a> north of Kigali; by 2006 these were providing 56% of the country's electricity, but were very costly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Resources_Report20115-215">[214]</a></sup> The government enacted a number of measures to alleviate this problem, including rehabilitating the Rugezi wetlands, which supply water to Burera and Ruhondo and investing in a scheme to extract methane gas from Lake Kivu, expected in its first phase to increase the country's power generation by 40%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfDB2011_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfDB2011-216">[215]</a></sup> Only 18% of the population had access to electricity in 2012, though this had risen from 10.8% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XIII)_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(XIII)-217">[216]</a></sup> The government's Economic Development and Poverty Reduction Strategy for 2013–18 aims to increase access to electricity to 70% of households by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaringanireMalikBanerjee20141_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaringanireMalikBanerjee20141-218">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government has increased investment in the <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Rwanda" title="Transport in Rwanda">transport infrastructure of Rwanda</a> since the 1994 genocide, with aid from the United States, <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, Japan, and others. The transport system consists primarily of the road network, with paved roads between Kigali and most other major cities and towns in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfDBOECD_Development_Centre2006439_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfDBOECD_Development_Centre2006439-219">[218]</a></sup> Rwanda is linked by road to other countries in the East African Community, namely Uganda, Tanzania, Burundi and <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, as well as to the eastern Congolese cities of <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bukavu" title="Bukavu">Bukavu</a>; the country's most important trade route is the road to the port of <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> via <a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">Kampala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, which is known as the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Corridor" title="Northern Corridor">Northern Corridor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETancott2014_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETancott2014-220">[219]</a></sup> The principal form of public transport in the country is the <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">minibus</a>, accounting for more than half of all passenger carrying capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334-221">[220]</a></sup> Some minibuses, particularly in Kigali,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201367_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201367-222">[221]</a></sup> operate an unscheduled service, under a <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">shared taxi</a> system,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201332_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201332-223">[222]</a></sup> while others run to a schedule, offering express routes between the major cities. There are a smaller number of large buses,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334-221">[220]</a></sup> which operate a scheduled service around the country. The principal private hire vehicle is the <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_taxi" title="Motorcycle taxi">motorcycle taxi</a>; in 2013 there were 9,609 registered motorcycle taxis in Rwanda, compared with just 579 <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicabs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334_221-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201334-221">[220]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coach_(vehicle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coach (vehicle)">Coach</a> services are available to various destinations in neighbouring countries. The country has an <a href="/wiki/Kigali_International_Airport" title="Kigali International Airport">international airport</a> at Kigali that serves several international destinations, the busiest routes being those to <a href="/wiki/JKIA" class="mw-redirect" title="JKIA">Nairobi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Entebbe_International_Airport" title="Entebbe International Airport">Entebbe</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECentre_For_Aviation2014_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentre_For_Aviation2014-224">[223]</a></sup> there is one domestic route, between Kigali and <a href="/wiki/Kamembe_Airport" title="Kamembe Airport">Kamembe Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Cyangugu" title="Cyangugu">Cyangugu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETumwebaze2015_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETumwebaze2015-225">[224]</a></sup> In 2017, construction began on the <a href="/wiki/Bugesera_International_Airport" title="Bugesera International Airport">Bugesera International Airport</a>, to the south of Kigali, which will become the country's largest when it opens, complementing the existing Kigali airport.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA2017_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA2017-226">[225]</a></sup> The national carrier is <a href="/wiki/RwandAir" title="RwandAir">RwandAir</a>, and the country is served by seven foreign airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECentre_For_Aviation2014_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentre_For_Aviation2014-224">[223]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the country has no railways, but there is a project underway, in conjunction with Burundi and Tanzania, to extend the Tanzanian <a href="/wiki/Central_Line_(Tanzania)" title="Central Line (Tanzania)">Central Line</a> into Rwanda; the three countries have invited expressions of interest from private firms to form a <a href="/wiki/Public_private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public private partnership">public private partnership</a> for the scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESenelwa2015_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESenelwa2015-227">[226]</a></sup> There is no public water transport between the port cities on Lake Kivu, although a limited private service exists and the government has initiated a programme to develop a full service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201343_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201343-228">[227]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Infrastructure_(Rwanda)" title="Ministry of Infrastructure (Rwanda)">Ministry of Infrastructure</a> is also investigating the feasibility of linking Rwanda to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> via shipping on the <a href="/wiki/Akagera_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Akagera River">Akagera River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201343_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMININFRA201343-228">[227]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Rwanda" title="Demographics of Rwanda">Demographics of Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Youth_in_Rwanda" title="Youth in Rwanda">Youth in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda" title="National Institute of Statistics of Rwanda">National Institute of Statistics of Rwanda</a> estimates Rwanda's population to be 11,262,564.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2015_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2015-229">[228]</a></sup> The 2012 census recorded a population of 10,515,973.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda20143_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda20143-4">[4]</a></sup> The population is young: in the 2012 census, 43.3% of the population were aged 15 and under, and 53.4% were between 16 and 64.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda20148_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda20148-230">[229]</a></sup> According to the CIA <i><a href="/wiki/World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a></i>, the annual birth rate is estimated at 40.2 births per 1,000 inhabitants in 2015, and the death rate at 14.9.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> The life expectancy is 67.67&nbsp;years (69.27&nbsp;years for females and 67.11&nbsp;years for males), which is the 26th lowest out of 224 countries and territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(III)2011_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(III)2011-231">[230]</a></sup> The overall sex ratio of the country is 95.9 males per 100 females.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting seven rural children, with a straw house and farmland in the background, taken in the Volcanoes National Park in 2005" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/220px-Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/330px-Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg/440px-Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_children_at_Volcans_National_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rural children
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 445 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,150/sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2015_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2015-229">[228]</a></sup> Rwanda's population density is amongst the highest in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanda2015_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanda2015-232">[231]</a></sup> Historians such as <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Prunier" title="Gérard Prunier">Gérard Prunier</a> believe that the 1994 genocide can be partly attributed to the population density.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier19954_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier19954-48">[47]</a></sup> The population is predominantly rural, with a few large towns; dwellings are evenly spread throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStraus2013215_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStraus2013215-233">[232]</a></sup> The only sparsely populated area of the country is the savanna land in the former province of <a href="/wiki/Umutara_Province" title="Umutara Province">Umutara</a> and Akagera National Park in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStreissguth200711_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStreissguth200711-234">[233]</a></sup> Kigali is the largest city, with a population of around one million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKigali_City_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKigali_City-235">[234]</a></sup> Its rapidly increasing population challenges its infrastructural development.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPercivalHomer-Dixon1995_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPercivalHomer-Dixon1995-236">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEREMA_(Chapter_2)2009_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEREMA_(Chapter_2)2009-237">[236]</a></sup> According to the 2012 census, the second largest city is <a href="/wiki/Gisenyi" title="Gisenyi">Gisenyi</a>, which lies adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a> and the Congolese city of <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a>, and has a population of 126,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECity_Population2012_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECity_Population2012-238">[237]</a></sup> Other major towns include <a href="/wiki/Ruhengeri" title="Ruhengeri">Ruhengeri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butare" title="Butare">Butare</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Muhanga" title="Muhanga">Muhanga</a>, all with populations below 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECity_Population2012_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECity_Population2012-238">[237]</a></sup> The urban population rose from 6% of the population in 1990,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPercivalHomer-Dixon1995_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPercivalHomer-Dixon1995-236">[235]</a></sup> to 16.6% in 2006;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201229_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201229-239">[238]</a></sup> by 2011, however, the proportion had dropped slightly, to 14.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201229_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201229-239">[238]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda has been a unified state since pre-colonial times,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppiahGates2010450_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppiahGates2010450-36">[35]</a></sup> and the population is drawn from just one cultural and linguistic group, the <a href="/wiki/Banyarwanda" title="Banyarwanda">Banyarwanda</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200252_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200252-240">[239]</a></sup> this contrasts with most modern African states, whose borders were drawn by <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">colonial powers</a> and did not correspond to ethnic boundaries or pre-colonial kingdoms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd19791_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd19791-241">[240]</a></sup> Within the Banyarwanda people, there are three separate groups, the Hutu, Tutsi and Twa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier19955_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier19955-242">[241]</a></sup> The CIA <i>World Factbook</i> gives estimates that the Hutu made up 84% of the population in 2009, the Tutsi 15% and Twa 1%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)_65-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_(I)-65">[64]</a></sup> The Twa are a pygmy people who descend from Rwanda's earliest inhabitants, but scholars do not agree on the origins of and differences between the Hutu and Tutsi.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200246–47_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200246–47-243">[242]</a></sup> Anthropologist Jean Hiernaux contends that the Tutsi are a separate race, with a tendency towards "long and narrow heads, faces and noses";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMamdani200247_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMamdani200247-244">[243]</a></sup> others, such as Villia Jefremovas, believe there is no discernible physical difference and the categories were not historically rigid.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJefremovas1995_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJefremovas1995-245">[244]</a></sup> In precolonial Rwanda the Tutsi were the ruling class, from whom the kings and the majority of chiefs were derived, while the Hutu were agriculturalists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier199511–12_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier199511–12-246">[245]</a></sup> The current <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Rwanda">government</a> discourages the Hutu/Tutsi/Twa distinction, and has removed such classification from identity cards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman2010_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman2010-247">[246]</a></sup> The 2002 census was the first since 1933<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKiwuwa201271_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKiwuwa201271-248">[247]</a></sup> which did not categorise Rwandan population into the three groups.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAgence_France-Presse2002_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAgence_France-Presse2002-249">[248]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Rwanda" title="Religion in Rwanda">Religion in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RwamaganaChurch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting the Roman Catholic parish church in Rwamagana, Eastern Province, including the main entrance, façade, the separate bell tower, and dirt forecourt" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/RwamaganaChurch.jpg/220px-RwamaganaChurch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/RwamaganaChurch.jpg/330px-RwamaganaChurch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/RwamaganaChurch.jpg/440px-RwamaganaChurch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2121" data-file-height="1412"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RwamaganaChurch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roman Catholic church in <a href="/wiki/Rwamagana" title="Rwamagana">Rwamagana</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The largest faith in Rwanda is <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Rwanda" title="Catholic Church in Rwanda">Roman Catholicism</a>, but there have been significant changes in the nation's religious demographics since the genocide, with many conversions to <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">evangelical</a> Christianity, and, to a lesser degree, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Rwanda" title="Islam in Rwanda">Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalkerApril_2004_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalkerApril_2004-250">[249]</a></sup> According to the 2012 census, Roman Catholics represented 43.7% of the population, Protestants (excluding <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a>) 37.7%, Seventh-day Adventists 11.8%, and Muslims 2.0%; 0.2% claimed no religious beliefs and 1.3% did not state a religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201417_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda201417-251">[250]</a></sup> Traditional religion, despite officially being followed by only 0.1% of the population, retains an influence. Many Rwandans view the <a href="/wiki/God_in_Christianity" title="God in Christianity">Christian God</a> as synonymous with the traditional Rwandan God <i><a href="/wiki/Imana" title="Imana">Imana</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWireduAbrahamIreleMenkiti2006236–237_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWireduAbrahamIreleMenkiti2006236–237-252">[251]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Rwanda" title="Languages of Rwanda">Languages of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's principal language is <a href="/wiki/Kinyarwanda" title="Kinyarwanda">Kinyarwanda</a>, which is spoken by nearly all Rwandans. The major European languages during the colonial era were <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, though it was never taught or widely used, and then <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, which was introduced by Belgium from 1916 and remained an official and widely spoken language after independence in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversité_Laval2010_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversité_Laval2010-253">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> was spoken too. The return of English-speaking Rwandan refugees in the 1990s<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversité_Laval2010_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversité_Laval2010-253">[252]</a></sup> added a new dimension to the country's linguistic diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESamuelsonFreedman2010_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESamuelsonFreedman2010-254">[253]</a></sup> Kinyarwanda, English, French, and Swahili are all official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup> Kinyarwanda is the national language while English is the primary medium of instruction in secondary and tertiary education. <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETabaro2015_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETabaro2015-256">[255]</a></sup> is also spoken by some as a second language, particularly returned refugees from Uganda, Kenya, Tanzania, and the Democratic Republic of Congo, and those who live along the border with the DRC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStanford_University_Swahili_Department_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStanford_University_Swahili_Department-257">[256]</a></sup> In 2015, Swahili was introduced as a mandatory subject in secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETabaro2015_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETabaro2015-256">[255]</a></sup> Inhabitants of Rwanda's <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nkombo_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nkombo Island (page does not exist)">Nkombo Island</a> speak <a href="/wiki/Mashi_language" title="Mashi language">Mashi</a>, a language closely related to Kinyarwanda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENakayima2010_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENakayima2010-258">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT">LGBT</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Rwanda" title="LGBT rights in Rwanda">LGBT rights in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Homosexuality is generally considered a <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">taboo</a> topic, and there is no significant public discussion of this issue in any region of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGmünder20071216_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGmünder20071216-259">[258]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Same-sex sexual activity is legal in Rwanda, and some cabinet-level government officials have expressed support for the rights of lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2016_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEU.S._Department_of_State2016-260">[259]</a></sup> However, Rwanda does not recognise same-sex marriages, civil unions or similar unions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_26_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECJCR2003article_26-261">[260]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Rwanda" title="Culture of Rwanda">Culture of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting two male dancers with straw wigs, neck garments, spears and sticks" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg/220px-Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg/330px-Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg/440px-Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1512" data-file-height="1671"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rwanda_IntoreDancers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Rwandan <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Intore (page does not exist)">intore</a></i> dancers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Rwanda" title="Music of Rwanda">Music</a> and dance are an integral part of Rwandan ceremonies, festivals, social gatherings and storytelling. The most famous traditional dance is a highly choreographed routine consisting of three components: the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umushagiriro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Umushagiriro (page does not exist)">umushagiriro</a></i>, or cow dance, performed by women;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERwanda_Development_Gateway_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERwanda_Development_Gateway-262">[261]</a></sup> the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Intore (page does not exist)">intore</a></i>, or dance of heroes, performed by men;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERwanda_Development_Gateway_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERwanda_Development_Gateway-262">[261]</a></sup> and the drumming, also traditionally performed by men, on drums known as <i>ingoma</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERMCA_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERMCA-263">[262]</a></sup> The best known dance group is the <a href="/wiki/National_Ballet_of_Rwanda" title="National Ballet of Rwanda">National Ballet</a>. It was established by President Habyarimana in 1974, and performs nationally and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggs2004_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggs2004-264">[263]</a></sup> Traditionally, music is transmitted orally, with styles varying between the social groups. Drums are of great importance; the royal drummers enjoyed high status within the court of the King (<i>Mwami</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle2007135–136_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle2007135–136-265">[264]</a></sup> Drummers play together in groups of varying sizes, usually between seven and nine in number.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle2007139_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle2007139-266">[265]</a></sup> The country has a growing popular music industry, influenced by African Great Lakes, Congolese, and American music. The most popular genre is <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>, with a blend of <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap">rap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ragga" title="Ragga">ragga</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMbabazi2008_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMbabazi2008-267">[266]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Igiseke.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting a bowl shaped off-white woven basket with tall conical lid and black zigzag pattern" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Igiseke.jpg/170px-Igiseke.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Igiseke.jpg/255px-Igiseke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Igiseke.jpg/340px-Igiseke.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1486" data-file-height="2331"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Igiseke.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rwandan woven <a href="/wiki/Agaseke" title="Agaseke">agaseke</a> basket
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional arts and crafts are produced throughout the country, although most originated as functional items rather than purely for decoration. Woven baskets and bowls are especially common, notably the basket style of the <a href="/wiki/Agaseke" title="Agaseke">agaseke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200768–70_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200768–70-268">[267]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Imigongo" title="Imigongo">Imigongo</a></i>, a unique cow dung art, is produced in the southeast of Rwanda, with a history dating back to when the region was part of the independent <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gisaka&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gisaka (page does not exist)">Gisaka</a> kingdom. The dung is mixed with natural soils of various colours and painted into patterned ridges to form geometric shapes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006243–244_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth2006243–244-269">[268]</a></sup> Other crafts include pottery and wood carving.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200631_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200631-270">[269]</a></sup> Traditional housing styles make use of locally available materials; circular or rectangular mud homes with grass-thatched roofs (known as <i>nyakatsi</i>) are the most common. The government has initiated a programme to replace these with more modern materials such as corrugated iron.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENtambara2009_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENtambara2009-271">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200775_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200775-272">[271]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda does not have a long history of written literature, but there is a strong oral tradition ranging from poetry to <a href="/wiki/Folk_stories" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk stories">folk stories</a>. Many of the country's moral values and details of history have been passed down through the generations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKing2007105_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKing2007105-273">[272]</a></sup> The most famous Rwandan literary figure was <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Kagame" title="Alexis Kagame">Alexis Kagame</a> (1912–1981), who carried out and published research into oral traditions as well as writing his own poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200629_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200629-274">[273]</a></sup> The Rwandan Genocide resulted in the emergence of a literature of witness accounts, essays and fiction by a new generation of writers such as <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Sehene" title="Benjamin Sehene">Benjamin Sehene</a>. A number of films have been produced about the Rwandan Genocide, including the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a>-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Hotel_Rwanda" title="Hotel Rwanda">Hotel Rwanda</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/100_Days_(2001_film)" title="100 Days (2001 film)">100 Days</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shake_Hands_with_the_Devil_(2007_film)" title="Shake Hands with the Devil (2007 film)">Shake Hands with the Devil</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sometimes_in_April" title="Sometimes in April">Sometimes in April</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Shooting_Dogs" title="Shooting Dogs">Shooting Dogs</a></i>, the last four having been filmed in Rwanda and having featured survivors as cast members.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilmo2006_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilmo2006-275">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFegley201655–56_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFegley201655–56-276">[275]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fourteen regular <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Rwanda" title="Public holidays in Rwanda">national holidays</a> are observed throughout the year,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Rwanda_(I)_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Rwanda_(I)-277">[276]</a></sup> with others occasionally inserted by the government. The week following Genocide Memorial Day on 7 April is designated an official week of mourning.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatsonRenziViggiani201025_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatsonRenziViggiani201025-278">[277]</a></sup> The victory for the RPF over the Hutu extremists is celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">Liberation Day</a> on 4 July. The last Saturday of each month is <i><a href="/wiki/Umuganda" title="Umuganda">umuganda</a></i>, a national morning of mandatory <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a> lasting from 8<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am to 11<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>am, during which all able bodied people between 18 and 65 are expected to carry out community tasks such as cleaning streets or building homes for vulnerable people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERwanda_Governance_Board_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERwanda_Governance_Board-279">[278]</a></sup> Most normal services close down during <i>umuganda</i>, and public transportation is limited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERwanda_Governance_Board_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERwanda_Governance_Board-279">[278]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Rwanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Rwanda">Cuisine of Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The cuisine of Rwanda is based on local <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple foods</a> produced by subsistence agriculture such as bananas, plantains (known as <i><a href="/wiki/Ibitoke" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibitoke">ibitoke</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Pulse_(legume)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulse (legume)">pulses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>, beans, and <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> (manioc).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781-280">[279]</a></sup> Many Rwandans do not eat meat more than a few times a month.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781-280">[279]</a></sup> For those who live near lakes and have access to fish, <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">tilapia</a> is popular.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781_280-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200781-280">[279]</a></sup> The potato, thought to have been introduced to Rwanda by German and Belgian <a href="/wiki/Second_European_colonization_wave_(19th_century%E2%80%9320th_century)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second European colonization wave (19th century–20th century)">colonialists</a>, is very popular.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713-281">[280]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a>, locally known as <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ubugari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ubugari (page does not exist)">Ubugari</a></i> (or <i>umutsima</i>) is common, a paste made from cassava or maize and water to form a <a href="/wiki/Porridge" title="Porridge">porridge</a>-like consistency that is eaten throughout the African Great Lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAuzias200774_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAuzias200774-282">[281]</a></sup> <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isombe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Isombe (page does not exist)">Isombe</a></i> is made from mashed cassava leaves and served with dried fish.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713-281">[280]</a></sup> Lunch is usually a buffet known as <i>mélange</i>, consisting of the above staples and sometimes meat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200654–55_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200654–55-283">[282]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brochette" class="mw-redirect" title="Brochette">Brochettes</a> are the most popular food when eating out in the evening, usually made from goat but sometimes <a href="/wiki/Tripe" title="Tripe">tripe</a>, beef, or fish.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200654–55_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200654–55-283">[282]</a></sup> In rural areas, many bars have a brochette seller responsible for tending and slaughtering the goats, skewering and <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">barbecuing</a> the meat, and serving it with grilled bananas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnyango2010_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnyango2010-284">[283]</a></sup> Milk, particularly in a fermented yoghurt form called <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ikivuguto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ikivuguto (page does not exist)">ikivuguto</a></i>, is a common drink throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENzabuheraheza2005_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENzabuheraheza2005-285">[284]</a></sup> Other drinks include a traditional beer called Ikigage made from sorghum and <i><a href="/wiki/Urwagwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Urwagwa">urwagwa</a></i>, made from bananas, which features in traditional rituals and ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713_281-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdekunle200713-281">[280]</a></sup> The major drinks manufacturer in Rwanda is <a href="/wiki/Bralirwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Bralirwa">Bralirwa</a>, which was established in the 1950s, a Heineken partner, and is now listed on the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan Stock Exchange">Rwandan Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(I)_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(I)-286">[285]</a></sup> Bralirwa manufactures <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drink</a> products from <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a>, under license, including <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fanta" title="Fanta">Fanta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(soft_drink)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprite (soft drink)">Sprite</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(II)_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(II)-287">[286]</a></sup> and a range of beers including <a href="/wiki/Primus_beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Primus beer">Primus</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCtzig_beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mützig beer">Mützig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amstel_Brewery" title="Amstel Brewery">Amstel</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turbo_King&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Turbo King (page does not exist)">Turbo King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(III)_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBralirwa_(III)-288">[287]</a></sup> In 2009 a new brewery, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brasseries_des_Mille_Collines&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brasseries des Mille Collines (page does not exist)">Brasseries des Mille Collines</a> (BMC) opened, manufacturing <a href="/wiki/Skol" title="Skol">Skol</a> beer and a local version known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Skol_Gatanu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Skol Gatanu (page does not exist)">Skol Gatanu</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENgarambe2012_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENgarambe2012-289">[288]</a></sup> BMC is now owned by Belgian company <a href="/wiki/Unibra" title="Unibra">Unibra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraig2012_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraig2012-290">[289]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_African_Breweries" title="East African Breweries">East African Breweries</a> also operate in the country, importing <a href="/wiki/Guinness" title="Guinness">Guinness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tusker_(beer)" title="Tusker (beer)">Tusker</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bell_(beer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bell (beer) (page does not exist)">Bell</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Whisky" title="Whisky">whisky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Distilled beverage">spirits</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKezio-Musoke2014_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKezio-Musoke2014-291">[290]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Rwanda" title="Sport in Rwanda">Sport in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg/220px-MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg/330px-MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg/440px-MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MTB_cycling_2012_Olympics_M_cross-country_RWA_Adrien_Niyonshuti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Adrien_Niyonshuti" title="Adrien Niyonshuti">Adrien Niyonshuti</a>, "one of the most famous people in Rwanda",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECyclingNews.com2012_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECyclingNews.com2012-292">[291]</a></sup> competing in the <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_mountain_biking" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross-country mountain biking">cross-country mountain biking</a> event at the 2012 Summer Olympics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Rwandan government, through its Sports Development Policy, promotes sport as a strong avenue for "development and peace building",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINISPOC201218_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINISPOC201218-293">[292]</a></sup> and the government has made commitments to advancing the use of sport for a variety of development objectives, including education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenColucci201486–90_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenColucci201486–90-294">[293]</a></sup> The most popular sports in Rwanda are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_sports" title="Paralympic
