sports">Paralympic sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENdengeye2014125–128_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENdengeye2014125–128-295">[294]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> has been growing in popularity,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAglietti2014_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAglietti2014-296">[295]</a></sup> as a result of refugees returned from Kenya, where they had learned to play the game.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(XI)2014_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_(XI)2014-297">[296]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">Cycling</a>, traditionally seen largely as a mode of transport in Rwanda, is also growing in popularity <a href="/wiki/Cycle_sport" title="Cycle sport">as a sport</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyeSmithNicholsonStewart2015206_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyeSmithNicholsonStewart2015206-298">[297]</a></sup> and Team Rwanda have been the subject of a book, <i>Land of Second Chances: The Impossible Rise of Rwanda's Cycling Team</i> and a film, <i><a href="/wiki/Rising_from_Ashes_(film)" title="Rising from Ashes (film)">Rising from Ashes</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobbins2013_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobbins2013-299">[298]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWillgoss2014_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWillgoss2014-300">[299]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwandans have been competing at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since 1984,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(I)2012_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(I)2012-301">[300]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_Games" title="Paralympic Games">Paralympic Games</a> since 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Paralympic_Committee2015_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Paralympic_Committee2015-302">[301]</a></sup> The country sent seven competitors to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London, representing it in athletics, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">mountain biking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(I)2012_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(I)2012-301">[300]</a></sup> and 15 competitors to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="2012 Summer Paralympics">London Summer Paralympics</a> to compete in athletics, <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_powerlifting" title="Paralympic powerlifting">powerlifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sitting_volleyball" title="Sitting volleyball">sitting volleyball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Paralympic_Committee2015_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Paralympic_Committee2015-302">[301]</a></sup> The country has also participated in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since joining the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(II)2010_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_Sport_(II)2010-303">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Prime_Minister2014_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Prime_Minister2014-304">[303]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwanda national basketball team">national basketball team</a> has been growing in prominence since the mid-2000s, with the men's team qualifying for the final stages of the <a href="/wiki/African_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="African Basketball Championship">African Basketball Championship</a> four times in a row since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBishumba2015_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBishumba2015-305">[304]</a></sup> The country bid unsuccessfully to host the <a href="/wiki/2013_African_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 African Basketball Championship">2013 tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackay2009_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackay2009-306">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Basketball_Federation2011_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Basketball_Federation2011-307">[306]</a></sup> Rwanda's <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_national_football_team" title="Rwanda national football team">national football team</a> has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> once, in the <a href="/wiki/2004_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2004 African Cup of Nations">2004 edition</a> of the tournament,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarlin2003_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarlin2003-308">[307]</a></sup> but narrowly failed to advance beyond the group stages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECopnall2004_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECopnall2004-309">[308]</a></sup> The team have failed to qualify for the competition since, and have never qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague201467_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague201467-310">[309]</a></sup> Rwanda's highest domestic football competition is the <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_National_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwanda National Football League">Rwanda National Football League</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMugabeKamasa2014_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMugabeKamasa2014-311">[310]</a></sup> as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the dominant team is <a href="/wiki/APR_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="APR FC">APR FC</a> of Kigali, having won 13 of the last 17 championships.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchöggl2015_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchöggl2015-312">[311]</a></sup> Rwandan clubs participate in the <a href="/wiki/Kagame_Interclub_Cup" title="Kagame Interclub Cup">Kagame Interclub Cup</a> for Central and East African teams, sponsored since 2002 by President Kagame.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECECAFA_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECECAFA-313">[312]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Rwanda" title="Education in Rwanda">Education in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG/220px-OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG/330px-OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG/440px-OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3128"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:OLPC_classroom_teaching.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Children in a Rwandan primary school, using laptops supplied by the <a href="/wiki/One_Laptop_Per_Child" class="mw-redirect" title="One Laptop Per Child">One Laptop Per Child</a> program
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Prior to 2012, the Rwandan government provided free education in state-run schools for nine years: six years in primary and three years following a common secondary programme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMINEDUC20102_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMINEDUC20102-314">[313]</a></sup> In 2012, this started to be expanded to 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015935_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015935-315">[314]</a></sup> A 2015 study suggests that while enrollment rates in primary schools are "near ubiquity", rates of completion are low and repetition rates high.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015931_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015931-316">[315]</a></sup> While schooling is fee-free, there is an expectation that parents should contribute to the cost of their children's education by providing them with materials, supporting teacher development and making a contribution to school construction. According to the government, these costs should not be a basis for the exclusion of children from education, however.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015935_315-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsAbbottMupenzi2015935-315">[314]</a></sup> There are many private schools across the country, some church-run, which follow the same syllabus but charge fees.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200627_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBriggsBooth200627-317">[316]</a></sup> From 1994 until 2009, secondary education was offered in either French or English; because of the country's increasing ties with the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, only the English syllabi are now offered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2009_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2009-318">[317]</a></sup> The country has a number of institutions of tertiary education. In 2013, the public <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rwanda" title="University of Rwanda">University of Rwanda</a> (UR) was created out of a merger of the former <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Rwanda" title="National University of Rwanda">National University of Rwanda</a> and the country's other public higher education institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoenig2014_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoenig2014-319">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacGregor2014_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacGregor2014-320">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERutayisire2013_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERutayisire2013-321">[320]</a></sup> In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> for tertiary education in Rwanda was 7.9%, from 3.6% in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(III)_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(III)-322">[321]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate, defined as those aged 15 or over who can read and write, was 71% in 2009, up from 38% in 1978 and 58% in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(I)_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(I)-323">[322]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Rwanda" title="Healthcare in Rwanda">Healthcare in Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Rwanda" title="Health in Rwanda">Health in Rwanda</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Butaro_Hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph depicting a hospital building, with Rwandan flag, viewed from the entrance pathway" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Butaro_Hospital.jpg/220px-Butaro_Hospital.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Butaro_Hospital.jpg/330px-Butaro_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Butaro_Hospital.jpg/440px-Butaro_Hospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3072"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Butaro_Hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Butaro_Hospital" title="Butaro Hospital">Butaro Hospital</a> at <a href="/wiki/Burera" class="mw-redirect" title="Burera">Burera</a>, Northern Province
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The quality of healthcare in Rwanda has historically been very low, both before and immediately after the 1994 genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrobacNaughton2014_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrobacNaughton2014-324">[323]</a></sup> In 1998, more than one in five children died before their fifth birthday,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(IV)_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(IV)-325">[324]</a></sup> often from <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBowdler2010_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBowdler2010-326">[325]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>President Kagame has made healthcare one of the priorities for the <a href="/wiki/Vision_2020_(Rwanda)" title="Vision 2020 (Rwanda)">Vision 2020</a> development programme,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2014_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2014-327">[326]</a></sup> boosting spending on health care to 6.5% of the country's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(V)_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(V)-328">[327]</a></sup> compared with 1.9% in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VI)_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VI)-329">[328]</a></sup> The government has devolved the financing and management of healthcare to local communities, through a system of health insurance providers called <i>mutuelles de santé</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWHO2008_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWHO2008-330">[329]</a></sup> The <i>mutuelles</i> were piloted in 1999, and were made available nationwide by the mid-2000s, with the assistance of international development partners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWHO2008_330-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWHO2008-330">[329]</a></sup> Premiums under the scheme were initially <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>2 per annum; since 2011 the rate has varied on a sliding scale, with the poorest paying nothing, and maximum premiums rising to US$8 per adult.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosenberg2012_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosenberg2012-331">[330]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rwanda&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 90% of the population was covered by the scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(II)2014_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(II)2014-332">[331]</a></sup> The government has also set up training institutes including the Kigali Health Institute (KHI), which was established in 1997<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIMF200034_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIMF200034-333">[332]</a></sup> and is now part of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rwanda" title="University of Rwanda">University of Rwanda</a>. In 2005, President Kagame also launched a program known as <i>The Presidents' Malaria Initiative</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[333]</a></sup> This initiative aimed to help get the most necessary materials for prevention of malaria to the most rural areas of Rwanda, such as mosquito nets and medication. </p>
      <p>In recent years Rwanda has seen improvement on a number of key health indicators. Between 2005 and 2013, life expectancy increased from 55.2 to 64.0,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VII)_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VII)-335">[334]</a></sup> under-5 mortality decreased from 106.4 to 52.0 per 1,000 live births,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VIII)_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(VIII)-336">[335]</a></sup> and incidence of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> has dropped from 101 to 69 per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(IX)_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Bank_(IX)-337">[336]</a></sup> The country's progress in healthcare has been cited by the international media and charities. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i> devoted an article to "Rwanda's Historic Health Recovery".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEmery2013_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEmery2013-338">[337]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Partners_In_Health" title="Partners In Health">Partners In Health</a> described the health gains "among the most dramatic the world has seen in the last 50 years".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosenberg2012_331-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosenberg2012-331">[330]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite these improvements, however, the country's health profile remains dominated by communicable diseases,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWHO2015_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWHO2015-339">[338]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> has described "significant health challenges",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015-340">[339]</a></sup> including the rate of maternal mortality, which it describes as "unacceptably high",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015_340-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015-340">[339]</a></sup> as well as the ongoing <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015_340-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSAID_(III)2015-340">[339]</a></sup> According to the American <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a>, travelers to Rwanda are highly recommended to take preventive malaria medication as well as make sure they are up to date with vaccines such as yellow fever.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[340]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rwanda also has a shortage of medical professionals, with only 0.84 physicians, nurses, and midwives per 1,000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPartners_In_Health2013_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPartners_In_Health2013-342">[341]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP) is monitoring the country's health progress towards <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> 4–6, which relate to healthcare. A mid-2015 UNDP report noted that the country was not on target to meet goal 4 on infant mortality, despite it having "fallen dramatically";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(II)2015_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(II)2015-343">[342]</a></sup> the country is "making good progress" towards goal 5, which is to reduce by three quarters the maternal mortality ratio,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(III)2015_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(III)2015-344">[343]</a></sup> while goal 6 is not yet met as <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Rwanda" title="HIV/AIDS in Rwanda">HIV prevalence</a> has not started falling.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(IV)2015_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_(IV)2015-345">[344]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>
